“Brain Trust” (not in textbook) - FDR’s advisers who crafted New Deal Programs
The Three R’s for the new deal (not in textbook) - Relief, recovery and reform
Relief - Feed, clothe, house and then put people to work right away.
- FERA, CCC, CWA, WPA, HOLC, NYA, Federal Arts Project, Federal Project No. 1
Recovery - help the economy and people recover, regain success (employment programs).
- AAA, NRA, TVA, IRA, PWA
Reform - Put system in place to make sure this type of catastrophe never happens again.
- SSA, Wagner Act (NLRA), Glass-Steagal Act, FHA, SEA, FDIC, FLSA
FLSA - Federal Labor Standards Act established minimum wage and no child labor after the
failure of the NRA/NIRA. (Think this as more for workers)
Wagner Act (NLRA) - basically replaced the NIRA by permanently protecting worker’s rights to
unionize and bargain collectively. (This this as more for unions)
Reconstruction Finance Corporation - Under Hoover, the corporation provided emergency
financing to banks, railroads and industries in the great depression.
Smoot Hawley Tariff - tariff by Hoover on 20k imported goods by 20-60%.
Repatriate - Deportation | Tydings McDuffie Act - Filipino Independence for 10 years, 50
Filipinos allowed to enter the US annually, extension of the 1924 immigration act | Filipino
Repatriation Act (‘35) - Paid passage for Filipinos to leave America.

Roosevelt’s Personality 662 - Very cheerful guy in the face of despair. In his inaugural address,
he said that Americans only needed to fear themselves and not other countries and promised to
take drastic actions against emergencies like war. He was the first president to make use of the
radio, where he explained his programs (like the emergency banking act) and plans to people
(called fireside chats) which boosted public confidence. He basically got respect for being one of
the boys. Journalists loved him so much that they didn’t take photos of him being paralyzed (so
the American public didn’t know about his polio).
TLDR: very popular with his fireside chats, cheerful personality, patriotism and booster of public
confidence.
“Bank Holiday” 662 - 2 days after taking office, FDR issued a proclamation stating that all
American banks close for 4 days until Congress could meet in a special session for bank
reforming. It helped relieve stress and 3 days later he passed the Emergency Banking Act,
which protected larger banks from being dragged down by weaknesses of smaller banks. It also
provided for Treasury Department inspection of all banks before they reopened. Congress was
pissed about this but within 3 days, the banking crisis ended. So yay.
TLDR: After taking office, FDR says American banks close for 4 days until Congress could
decide on bank reforms. 3 days later, the Emergency Banking Act gets passed which protects
larger banks from being dragged down by smaller ones. Within 3 days the banking crisis ended.

[PAGE 188]
Economy Act (added this myself) - After the Emergency Banking Act, FDR sends the Economy
Act which convinced conservatives (business guys especially) that the fed gov was in safe,
responsible hands. It balanced the federal budget by cutting the salaries of government
employees and reduced pensions to vets by 15%.
TLDR: Economy Act - FDR uses the Economy Act to convince businesses and conservatives
that the fed gov was in good hands. It cut salaries of government employees and reduced
pensions to vets by 15%.
Prohibition Repealed 663 - Now sale and manufacture of beer is legalized with a 3.2% alcohol
content. The 21nd amendment (to kill prohibition) passed in 1933.
AAA 663 - Agricultural Adjustment Act (1933) passed to reduce crop production to end over
supply of agriculture and reduce inflation of farm prices. Through the Agricultural Adjustment
Administration (Yes, the AAA), farmers could decide on production limits for their crops, and the
AAA would tell the farmer how much they should produce. Adding on, the AAA would pay them
subsidies for the land not being used. Income increased by ½ and made the agricultural
economy stable. The AAA favored larger farmers over smaller ones.
TLDR: Agricultural Adjustment Act is passed to end overproduction of agriculture and deflate
prices. The Agricultural Adjustment Administration would pay them subsidies for unused land.
Income increased by a half and made the agriculture economy stable.
“Rural Electrification” 663 - Poor farmers also got help. The Resettlement Administration (1935)
and its successor, the Farm Security Administration (1937) gave loans to farmers so they could
relocate to better lands. But it only moved less than 1k farmers. More effective was the Rural
Electrification Administration (1935) which made electric power available for the first time to
many farmers.
TLDR: Rural Electrification - Rural Electrification Administration (‘35) gave electricity for the first
time to many farmers.
NRA 666 - Thanks to Roosevelt, the National Industrial Recovery Act (‘33) gets passed because
business leaders don’t enjoy workers being pissed at low salaries and high prices and they also
hate antitrust laws (so those get relieved). The National Recovery Administration, the agency for
this act, had a leader named Hugh S. Johnson (very interesting name) who told every business
to accept a temporary “blanket code”: minimum wage between 30 and 40 cents an hour with
max workweek of 35-40 hrs + abolition of child labor, so many people agreed with it.
Unfortunately, the codes were poorly and hastily written and the fed officials had no experience
running such a big program. Big companies manipulated the rules of the NIRA to work to their
advantage at the expense of small businesses.

[PAGE 189]
TLDR: The National Recovery Administration runs the National Industrial Recovery Act (NIRA)
and is led by Huge Johnson I mean Hugh S. Johnson who said everyone in business should
accept a “blanket code” which made minimum wage 30-40c/hour with max workweek 35-40 hrs
+ no more child labor. Cuz the rules were poorly written and fed officials had no experience
running the program, big companies manipulated the rules to work in their favor.
Section 7(a) 666 - Section 7(a) of the NIRA said workers could form unions and engage in
collective bargaining and encouraged others to do the same. BUT, it had no ways to enforce
said terms. Thus, employers ignored it and increased wages were not recognized as well. The
Public WOrks Administration (PWA, 1933) which was to execute orders from the NIRA’s
spending programs was very slow at spending funds and it didn’t help the economy fast
enough. Industrial production fell after the NRA began. Schechter Poultry Corp v. United States
case led to the Supreme Court to declare the NIRA unconstitutional which ended the program.
By the way, the PWA funded large scale public works (construction) to boost the economy.
TLDR: Section 7a of the NIRA said workers could form unions, but had no way to enforce the
terms. Employers ignored the NIRA and the PWA’s execution of the NIRA was very slow and it
couldn’t help the economy. The NRA failed at industrial production and Schechter Poultry Corp
v. The United States ended the NIRA.
TVA 66b7 - After the AAA and NRA supported economic planning but let farmers and business
leaders stay in control, reformers got mad and said the fed gov should control planning directly.
The solution? - The TVA (Tennessee Valley Authority 1933) focused on regional planning and
cheap electricity for farmers. It built dams, prevented flooding, improved transportation, and
encouraged industry in the Tennessee Valley. The TVA didn’t challenge racial discrimination.
TLDR: Tennessee Valley Authority gives cheap electricity to farmers. It built dams, prevented
flooding, improved transportation and encouraged industry in the Tennessee Valley.
Glass-Steagall Act 668 - The early New Deal expanded federal control over the economy. The
Glass-Steagall Act regulated banks, separated commercial banking and investment banking,
and created the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC), which insured bank deposits up
to $2,500. In 1935, a new banking law gave more power to the Federal Reserve Board in
Washington, strengthening federal control over banking .
TLDR: Glass-Steagall Act regulated banks, separated commercial and investment banks and
made the Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation to insure bank deposits.
SEC 668 - To protect investors, Congress passed the Securities Act of 1933, which required
companies to give full and accurate information about new stocks. In 1934, it created the
Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) to regulate and monitor the stock market. These
laws increased government oversight after scandals and criminal trials damaged public trust in
Wall Street.

[PAGE 190]
TLDR: Through the Securities Act, the SEC will now police the stock market to increase gov
oversight after scandals that damaged public confidence in Wall Street.
CWA 668 - FDR creates the Federal Emergency Relief Administration (FERA) to give cash to
states for relief, led by Harry Hopkins. However, Roosevelt preferred work relief instead of direct
handouts. So the Civil Works Administration (CWA) was created, providing over 4 million
temporary jobs building roads, schools, and parks to boost the economy and help the
unemployed.
TLDR: CWA is created to provide jobs for building roads, schools and parks to boost the
economy and help the unemployed. FERA gave cash to states for relief.
CCC 668 - FDR strongly supported the Civilian Conservation Corps (CCC), which gave young
unemployed men jobs in parks and forests doing conservation work; however, camps were
racially segregated.
To help struggling farmers and homeowners, the gov created the Farm Credit Administration
and passed the Frazier-Lemke Farm Bankruptcy Act to help farmers keep their land. It also
established the Home Owners' Loan Corporation to refinance home mortgages and later the
Federal Housing Administration (FHA) to insure home loans.
TLDR: Civilian Conservation Corps gave young unemployed men jobs in parks and forests for
racially segregated conservation work.
Farm Credit Administration - passed the Frazier-Lemke Farm Bankruptcy act to help farmers
keep their land
Home Owners Loan Corporation (HOLC) - Refinance home mortgages
Federal Housing Administration (FHA) - insured home loans
American Liberty League 669 - By 1934, critics on both the right and left strongly attacked the
New Deal. Wealthy conservatives, including the Du Pont family, formed the American Liberty
League to oppose FDR’s policies, calling them too powerful and anti-business, but the group
gained little support beyond industrial leaders. Radical groups like the Communist Party USA
and the Socialist Party of America also criticized the New Deal, yet they failed to gain
widespread public support.
TLDR: Wealthy conservatives form the unpopular American Liberty League which opposes FDR
cuz they are too anti-business. Unpopular radical groups like the Communist Party USA and the
Socialist Party also criticize the New Deal.
Townsend Plan 669 - During the New Deal, some powerful political movements challenged
Roosevelt from outside the usual left–right spectrum. Dr. Francis Townsend proposed giving
Americans aged 60+ a $200 monthly pension if they retired and spent the $200, gaining over 5
million supporters; although Congress rejected his plan, it helped build support for the 1935
Social Security Act. Father Charles Coughlin, a popular radio priest from Michigan, who liked

[PAGE 191]
Roosevelt but later criticized him and promoted major banking and currency reforms. He
founded the National Union for Social Justice in 1935 and had one of the largest radio
audiences in the country. The NUSJ hated jews and communism and capitalism and ensured
economic well-being for the entire community.
TLDR: The Townsend Plan - Francis Townsend said we should give 60+ y.o Americans a $200
monthly pension. Congress rejected the plan but it built support for the 1935 Social Security Act.
Father Charles Coughlin founded the National Union for Social Justice in 1935 and has the
largest radio audiences in the country. The NUSJ hated capitalism and communism and
ensured economic well-being for the entire community.
Huey Long 670 - Senator Huey P. Long of Louisiana becomes a big threat to the New Deal. He
attacks his opponents (banks, oil companies and political elites) which leads to people calling
him a dictator. He remains very popular cuz he builds roads, schools and hospitals. He also
revised tax codes, distributing free textbooks & lowered utility rates. In 1930, he was elected to
the US senate which increased his national influence.
TLDR: Huey Long threatens the new deal by attacking banks, oil companies and political elites.
People call him a dictator but he remains popular cuz he builds roads, schools, hospitals,
revised tax codes, distributed free textbooks and lowered utility rates. In 1930 he was elected to
the US senate.
Share-Our-Wealth Society 670 - At first, Huey Long actually supported FDR but in 1932 broke
relations. He opposed the New Deal and created the Share-Our-Wealth Plan, which said: tax
the rich and redistribute their money to make sure every family has a 5k allowance and a 2-2.5k
salary. In 1934, he formed the Share Our Wealth Society which gained much support. By 1935,
the polls showed that he could win over 10% of the vote, which possibly could have affected
presidential elections.
TLDR: Huey Long creates the Share-Our-Wealth Plan which taxed the rich to distribute the
money to make sure every family had a 5k homestead allowance and a 2.5k salary.
National Labor Relations Board 670 - FDR launches the second new deal to deal with the Great
Depression and political pressure. He becomes more critical of big businesses and begins to
support the Public Utility Holding Company Act of 1935 which limits large utility companies. He
proposes higher, more progressive taxes on the wealthy too. After the Supreme Court struck
down the National Industrial Recovery Act, Congress passed the National Labor Relations Act
of 1935 which created the National Labor RElations Board to protect worker’s rights to form
unions and bargain collectively.
TDLR: National Labor Relations Board - protected workers rights to form unions.
Industrial Unionism 671 - The AFL supports craft unions, which organize workers by specific
skills. But many workers are unskilled at the time so industrial unionism becomes popular. It

[PAGE 192]
basically just organizes all workers in the same industry into one union no matter their job,
which increases a worker’s overall productivity.
TLDR: Industrial Unionism basically organizes all workers in the same industry into one union
no matter the job to boost productivity.
CIO 671 - Many AFL leaders opposed industrial unionism (above term) but John L.Lewis
supported it. After conflicts with the AFL leaders, Lewis decided to form the Committee of
Industrial Organization which became the Congress of Industrial Organization (CIO) in 1936.
The CIO organized all workers in an industry and welcomed women and African Americans and
used more aggressive tactics to unionize major industries like steel and automobiles.
TLDR: John L.Lewis forms the Congress of Industrial Organization after conflicts with AFL
leaders. It aggressively unionized the steel and automobile industry and organized all works in
an industry and welcomed women and African Americans.
Sit-Down Strike 671 - The United Auto Workers (UAW) became popular in 1937 after workers
led a sit-down strike at General Motors by occupying factories and refusing to leave. Michigan
governor Frank Murphy refused to remove them and GM recognized the union. Sit-down strikes
later ended cuz they were seen as illegal. In the steel industry, U.S. Steel recognized unions
peacefully but smaller companies resisted the unions. During the 1937 Memorial Day Massacre,
police killed 10 striking workers and the steel strike failed.
TLDR: United Auto Workers lead a sit-down strike at GM. Steel industry recognized unions, but
small companies didn’t. During the 1937 memorial day massacre, police kill 10 workers and
steel strikes failed.
Organized Labor’s Rapid Growth 671 - After 1937, unions grew a lot. There were 4720 strikes
that year and 80% ended in favor of unions. Union membership increased from 3 million in 1932
to 8 million in 1937 and reached 10 million by 1941, including workers in the steel industry
whose employers eventually recognized unions like the SWOC (Steel Workers Organizing
committee).
TLDR: Unions grow a lot during the late 30s, Unions win a lot of strikes and gain a lot of
members. Yeah, that’s it.
Unemployment Insurance 672 - FDR supports the Social Security Act in 1935, which creates
pensions for old people, which is just unemployment insurance and aid for people with
disabilities and dependent children. Workers and employers paid payroll taxes to fund these
retirement benefits, but the payments were small at first and some groups like domestic and
agricultural workers were excluded. The SSA tried to create an insurance system rather than
simple welfare and became the foundation of America’s long-term social security system.

[PAGE 193]
TLDR: The Social Security Act created unemployment insurance (funded by employers and
workers) to aid old people, disabled people and dependent children. At first the payments were
small and domestic/agricultural workers were excluded.
WPA 673 - The Works Progress Administration was created in 1935 by FDR (why tf do I keep
on mentioning him he’s basically responsible for 100% of all of these acts) to give jobs to
unemployed Americans during the Great Depression. Harry Hopkins led the administration and
he was able to hire millions to build public buildings, roads, bridges and airports. The
Administration also supported artists and writers through special programs and helped young
people through the National Youth Administration. Most job programs mainly helped men, but
women received cash aid for dependent children.
TLDR: Led by Harry Hopkins, the Workers Progress Administration is created to give jobs to
unemployed people during the GD. Work included: building buildings, roads, bridges and
airports. It supported artists and writers. NYA helped young people.
Alf Landon 673 - By 1936, as the economy improved, FDR was likely to win reelection due to
his New Deal. Republicans nominated Alf Landon, but he ran a weak campaign. Opposition
weakened after Huey Long was assassinated in 1935, and the new Union Party failed to gain
support. Roosevelt won a historic landslide, earning about 61% of the vote and carrying every
state except Maine and Vermont, while Democrats strengthened their control of Congress.
TLDR: Republican Alf London - he loses to FDR cuz London’s campaign is weak and FDR
established his superiority through the New Deal.
Electoral Realignment 675 - The 1936 election showed a major party realignment caused by the
New Deal. The Democratic Party built a strong coalition of Western and Southern farmers,
urban workers, the poor, unemployed people, Black voters in Northern cities, progressives, and
liberals. This broad support gave Democrats a long-lasting majority, and it took Republicans
many decades to build a majority coalition again.
TLDR: The 1936 election saw new people supporting different parties. Poor, unemployed
people, African Americans in the North, urban workers, progressives and liberals supported the
Democrats. It took a long time for republicans to gain a majority vote.
Court Packing 675 - After winning reelection in 1936, FDR tried to limit the power of the
conservative Supreme Court of the United States, which had struck down New Deal laws like
the National Industrial Recovery Act and the Agricultural Adjustment Act. In 1937, he proposed
the “Court-packing plan” to add up to six new justices, but Congress rejected it after the Court
began upholding New Deal laws in cases like West Coast Hotel Co. v. Parrish. Although the
Court became more supportive of New Deal reforms, the failed plan hurt Roosevelt politically
and increased opposition from conservatives.

[PAGE 194]
TLDR: In order to limit the power of the Supreme Court (cuz they struck down on ND laws like
the NIRA and AAA), FDR created the Court Packing plan - which added 6 new justices (which
Congress rejected). The failed plan hurt Roosevelt, and conservatives increased their hate
towards FDR.
Roosevelt Recession 678 - The “Roosevelt Recession” of 1937 was blamed on reduced gov
spending. In 1938, FDR asks Congress for 5 billion for public works and relief, which restarts
the economic recovery and supports the idea of gov spending to fight recessions. He also
pushed stronger antitrust actions, leading to the creation of the Temporary National Economic
Committee and more aggressive enforcement. In 1938, Congress passed the Fair Labor
Standards Act, which created a national minimum wage, a 40-hour workweek, and limits on
child labor, though it excluded many women and minority workers at first.
TLDR: Roosevelt Recession of 1937 is blamed on reduced gov spending. The Temporary
National Economic Committee is made for antitrust. Congress passes the Fair Labor Standards
Act to create national minimum wage, 40 hour workweek and no child labor (not for women or
minorities).
End of the New Deal 678 - By the end of 1938, the New Deal had mostly ended because
Congress opposed new major reforms. Franklin D. Roosevelt also began focusing more on
preparing the United States for possible war as global tensions increased, shifting attention
away from domestic reform.
TLDR: ND ended in 1938 cuz Congress opposed new reforms. FDR begins to prepare the US
for war and focuses less on domestic reform.

state, because of all the relief programs. Conservatives were pretty focused on making sure
welfare would not have that big of an impact, and also reinforce some discrimination though…

New Expectations of Government 684 The New deal greatly impacted the people’s expectations
of what a government should be doing for the people. First of all, the democratic party became

matters, meaning the people expected their candidates to actually support them economically.

Washington Conference of 1921 687 The Washington Conference was an attempt to prevent
war by reducing the amount of naval armaments there were in the world. THe proposal limited
the amount of total naval armaments and set a ratio of arms nations could have. This
inadvertently gave Japan a ton of “legal rights” to their imperialist campaign, as Japan had been

The Dawes plan was a plan for European economic recovery to fix the main problems that
happened to the world economies after WWI
1. Britain and France are broke
2. Germany is also broke, but they also have to pay reparations to France and Britain
3. Germany is like really really really broke
So the plan was that Americans would give loans to the Germans to help them recover and
build an economy, and in turn France and Britain would reduce to total amount of debt Germany
had
The Plan didn’t really work due to the fact that the Banks used this as an opportunity to make

Also people pointed out that this put billions of dollars into the hands of a very unstable Europe.

War-Induced Economic Recovery 709 WWII for Americans was the final push out of the Great

Union Gains 712 Ironically enough, WWII was so successful in helping the US economy that

shortage(meaning not enough people to work the given jobs) because of how many men and
women were employed to work in the military (over 15 million). As such, Union membership
rose from 10 to 13 million in just 4 years between 1941-1945. The government then issued a
limit on how much wage increases for workers could be (15% max), but also issued a guarantee
that new employees would be automatically enrolled into unions. This was overall negative for
the American Unions, and many Americans went on strike.
Office of Price Administration 712 Government passed the Anti-Inflation Act which gave the
government a LOT of control over the economy, giving them the power to freeze prices, wages,
and rent anywhere in the country. The act was to be enforced by the Office of Price
Administrations. This helped the US economy not enter a state of inflation similar to that of WWI
in WWII, but for obvious reasons was not entirely popular with the general populace. After all,
nobody wants to get their wages frozen.
War Production Board 713 War Production Board was an organization that was pressured by
the public to be formed by the president. It would handle wartime economic growth and had
similar power to the War Industries Board in WWI. The WPB was pretty shit at its job and
couldn’t really get anything to work, but luckily for the US, the economy was fine without the
WPB’s help.

scientist Vannevar Bush for military research and development because Axis powers had much

Debating of the Bomb’s Use 727 This point is more retrospective than actual historical event
stuff, but the usage of the Atomic Bomb on Japan (twice) was and is heavily debated.
The main arguing points are
● Should the bomb have been used
○ Some argued that Japan was not going to surrender unless something really big
happened, and that the moderates in Japan that wanted to surrender didn’t even
have the power to do so anyway. Japan’s whole imperialistic track record didn’t
do anyone favors, and the kamikazes also implanted the idea that Japan would
fight until the end at any cost. Also the people in this group tended to argue that
the usage of the bomb would prevent a costly invasion of the entirety of Japan.
○ The other group of people were scared about the repercussions of using such a
massive weapon, fearing the aftermath and political repercussions on using the
bomb. I would say more but the book really didn’t add much else.
● Why was the bomb really used (cold war politics?)
○ Some argue that Truman wanted to use the bomb to end the war quickly by
forcing the Japanese to give up
○ While others argue it was more of a show of power to Russia, and to intimidate
Stalin.
Well whatever the reasoning really was, On the record Truman pretty much wrote that he had a

Truman”s Fair Deal 742 After the surrender of Japan, Truman submitted his 21 point Fair Deal
program to Congress. This would expand Social Security, raise the minimum wage by over
50%, and help with unemployment through rigorous government spending. In addition, he also
argued for a public housing and environmental project, and the government promoted scientific
research. Most important of all: national health insurance. The Fair Deal went into motion, and
although its intentions were good, the Fair Deal was stopped by conservatives who were very
absolute on lowering government spending, meaning that the Fair Deal had less money to work
with.
TLDR: Truman proposes the Fair Deal, which is New Deal 2.0 but with some more added
benefits but conservatives don’t like spending government money so the deal doesn’t go
through.

since this was heavily publicized, and also his position as a senator made it very serious when
such an accusation was made. McCarthy then went on a RAMPAGE accusing just about
anybody of communism. People of all different backgrounds were put under scrutiny. If your
ethnicity was one that was “associated” with communism, Russian, Chinese, Etc, you were
probably seen as a communist. During this time of fear, you could be locked up, out of a job, or
put down as a criminal just for holding any sort of trait that could be associated with
communism.

Goverment Spending 754 During the period up from WWII’s end to the 1960s, the US
experienced an economic boom of GDP growth of 250%, unemployment rates drilled into the

a bunch of this new money to build infrastructure. Schools were built, veterans got welfare, and
highways were sprouting up like weeds. Far and away however, was the growth of the military.
The US was gearing up for a possible war between the US and the USSR, and as such they
would enter such an arms race.

Echo Park 766 Echo Park was a valley in the Dinosaur National Monument, it was a place that
became a hot topic in the 1950s. In the early 1950s, the federal government’s Bureau of
Reclamation proposed building a dam across the Green River, which runs through Echo Valley,
to create a lake for recreation and a source of hydroelectric power. This made the American
environmental movement, which had been quiet after its defeat at Hetch Hetchy Valley, come
back from its slumber.
TLDR - Echo Park was a valley in Dinosaur National Monument that became controversial in
the 50s when the gov decided to build a dam on the Green River to implement hydroelectricity
and make a recreational lake. It makes the environmentalists mad, which revives the
environmentalist movement after they got shit on at Hetch Hetchy Valley a while back.

controversy helped elevate a new leader, David Brower, who transformed the club into the
nation’s leading environmental organization.
TLDR - The Sierra Club becomes active again after the Echo Park controversy. Led by David
Brower, it transformed the Sierra Club into the nation’s major force in the environmental
movement.

showcase their artists. These payments, which became known as “payola,” produced a brief but

Declining Agricultural prices 770 Farmers are struggling to make ends meet in the 50s. In 1948,
they had received 8.9 percent of the national income, and in 1956, they received only 4.1
percent. This is in part due to the shrinking farm population. In just 1956, almost 10 percent of
the rural population moved into or was absorbed by cities. Also, because of enormous surpluses
in basic stables, prices fell 33 percent in those years.

Black Urban Migration 771 As white families moved from cities to suburbs, many inner city
neighborhoods became vast repositories for the poor, “ghettos” from which there was no easy
escape. The growth of these neighborhoods owed much to a vast migration of African
Americans out of the countryside and into industrial cities. More than 3 million black men and
women moved from the South to northern cities between 1940 and 1960. Similar migrations
from Mexico and Puerto Rico expanded poor Hispanic neighborhoods at the same time.

Federal Highway Act of 1956 The Federal Highway Act authorized 25 billion dollars for a ten
year project that built over 40,000 miles of interstate highways, the largest public works project
in American history. The program was to be funded through a highway “trust fund,” whose
revenues would come from new taxes on the purchase of fuel, automobiles, trucks, and tires.

Brown V Board of Education 772 In considering the legal segregation of a Kansas public school
system, the Court rejected its own 1896 Plessy v Ferguson which barred Black Americans from
entering segregated schools not meant for African Americans decision in the Brown v Board of
Education case. This decision was the culmination of many decades of effort by black
opponents of segregation, including a group of NAACP lawyers who trained at Howard
University under Charles Houston.

[PAGE 220]
Separate But Equal Doctrine Overturned 772 In Topeka Kansas, an African American girl that
lived right next to an white elementary school was forced to drive miles to a segregated public
school in order to get her an education. This was brought up to the supreme court where they
found that access to public education needs to be more equal and as such, the separate but
equal doctrine was overturned. This was followed up in 1954 when the Supreme Court released
another decision that urged schools to desegregate ASAP. So Big Ws.
Massive Resistance 772 In some communities, compliance came relatively quickly and quietly.
More often, however, strong local opposition produced long delays and bitter conflicts. Some
school districts ignored the ruling altogether, while others attempted to circumvent it with purely
toke efforts to integrate. More than 100 southern members of Congress signed a “manifesto” in
1956 denouncing the Brown decision and urged their constituents to defy it.
TLDR - After Brown v Board of education, many southern whites opposed it. Some states
refused to comply, delayed integration or signed the 1956 "Southern Manifesto" which resisted
ruling.
Little Rock 773 President Eisenhower met the Brown decision with skepticism, and once said it
had set back progress on race relations “at least fifteen years”. But in September 1957, he
faced a case of direct state defiance of federal authority and had to act. An angry white mob
tried to prevent implementation of the Brown decision by blockading the entrances to the school,
and the Governor refused to do anything to stop it. Eisenhower responded by mobilizing the
National Guard and sending troops to Little Rock.(This should sound familiar)
TLDR - In 1957, 9 African American students tried to go to a high school in Little Rock but faced
violent resistance. Dwight D. Eisenhower sent the National Guard to enforce the integration
after the governor refused.
Montgomery Bus Boycott 773 Rosa Parks, which you guys have all heard of, started the
Montgomery Bus Boycott when she refused to give up her seat to a white passenger in 1955 on
a Montgomery bus. When she was forced to move, African American communities nearby
caught wind and started the Montgomery Bus Boycott, a boycott in which Black citizens opted to
either walk or bike to and from work, reducing a major source of income from the Bus, leading to
the desegregation of busses in Montgomery when economic pressure started to sink in on
Montgomery.
MLK’s Strategy 773 King’s approach to black protest was based on nonviolence. He took from
the teachings of Mahatma Gandhi, Henry David Thoreau and from the Christian doctrine. He
produced an approach to racial struggle that captured the moral high ground for his supporters.
He urged African Americans to engage in peaceful demonstrations and to respond to hate with
love.

Freedom Rides 786 Freedom Rides were a tactic endorsed by the CORE (Congress of Racial
Equality) that fought against the segregation of Buses in the south. Freedom Riders tried to
force the desegregation of buses by riding interstate buses into the segregated South, and were
met with savage enough violence that JFK had to send in the army and also pass laws
integrating buses and trains.
This led to the SNCC and other organizations fighting against segregation with greater strength
and conviction.

Surging Latino Immigration 816 Latino/Hispanic Americans were the fastest growing minority group
in the US, with some Latino Americans being in the US since the Mexican American War. Others
immigrated during WWII with the Bracero Program. Even after the war, many Mexican Americans
continued to enter the US undocumented. However in the 1960s and 70s, the amount of Mexican
Americans had surged, beginning to outnumber African Americans.
“Chicano” Activism 816 Partly due to Language barriers and the Family Centered Mexican Culture
that many immigrants held, Latino Unions grew very slowly at first, but in the 1960s, Younger
Mexican Americans began to call themselves Chicanos as a way of emphasizing the shared culture
of Spanish Speaking Americans. Chicanos often advocated for what was basically a Mexican
version of the Black Power movement.

against growers and fight for increased wages. At the time, many Southern California farmers often
paid Latino workers pretty much nothing and had them working in what was basically slavery with a

“Stonewall Riot” 817 Another important minority group that began to openly fight for rights and
recognition was the LGBTQ+ Community.
The Stonewall Inn was a bar in New York City that was notable for it’s LGBTQ+ patrons. On June 27
1969, the Police decided to raid the bar and arrest everyone for the crime of being gay (they
assumed everyone in the bar was gay). At this point everyone was fed up with the police harassing
the bar, and this led to the police being attacked, and then someone started a fire in the Stonewall
Inn, and then things escalated into a Riot.
The Stonewall Riot really made the Gay Liberation Movement public thing, with new organizations
springing up in the wake of the Riots. In addition, Public discussion on LGBTQ+ stuff became a lot
less taboo and more openly discussed.
Impact of the Gay Liberation Movement 818 The Gay liberation movement led to a lot of people
gaining the strength to only come out as gay and demand the recognition of gay relationships as
legitimate. Even through the AIDS epidemic and other events, the LGBTQ+ gained several legal
victories. In the 1990s especially, there were many wins and a couple losses for the LGBTQ+
community. For example, the “Don’t Ask Don’t Tell” Policy was created as a weak compromise
between the Military and the LGBTQ Community.

The book brought mass attention across the US about the state of women’s role in society in the
suburban age, either through newfound support or extreme criticism.

workplaces (Wage gap still exists), especially the fact that women couldn’t work in a lot of
industries.

“Hearts and Minds” 799 The “pacification” program, intended to push the Viet Cong from areas

Growing Opposition to War 800 By the end of 1967, American students who opposed the war
had become a significant political force. Peace marches in New York, Washington DC, and other
cities drew broad attention to the antiwar movement. Opposition to the war became a central
issue in left-wing politics and in the culture of colleges and universities.
War-Induced Inflation 800 Johnson’s commitment to fighting the war while continuing his Great
Society reforms(“Guns and butter”) proved to be impossible to maintain. The inflation rate rose
from 2 percent to 6 percent in just two years. In order to combat this, Johnson asked for a tax
increase which was necessary to stop inflation from growing, and in return conservatives
received a six billion dollar reduction in Great Society funding.

legacy”, a set of ideas that, for a time, was central to American liberalism.

powerless. The passions Kennedy aroused made his violent death a particularly shattering

Baker v. Carr 829 Baker V Carr was a court case by the Warren Court, which was what they
called the currently pretty Liberal Supreme Court. This case required electoral districts to be
portioned so each vote had equal weight among all voters in a State. At the time, rural areas

“Right-to-Life” Movement 866 Opposition to abortion was creating a powerful grassroots
movement. The right-to-life movement, as it called itself, found its most fervent supporters
among Catholics; and the Catholic Church itself lent its institutional authority to the battle
against legalized abortion.
“Pro-Choice” Movement 867 Pro-Choice wasn’t really about abortion since abortion was already
legalized, but more about the social right for women to decide whether or not to keep a child or
not (it is them that have to endure 9 months after all). Clinton was pretty pro-abortion/pro-choice
so for a good period the Pro-Choice movement got a lot of attraction, but afterwards in the Bush
administration it became increasingly risky since Bush was openly anti-abortion.
Human Genome Project 863 In 89, the US government approved 3 billion dollars to go to the
Human Genome Project, which would try to analyze and reproduce human genes.
